#  On Startup                        #
######################################

start_at                 = your_zedroom
loading_screen = loading_screen


on_startup {

: ask_bool {

   var      = tune
   question = Do you wish to see the introduction?
}
: if (tune) {
 : clear_screen;
 


: print_graphic "ladybird" ;


  
                   : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
    : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
      : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
       : beep millis = "400"  pitch = "-26" ;
       : beep millis = "400"  pitch = "-26" ;
         : beep millis = "225"  pitch = "-26";
          : beep millis = "225"  pitch = "-26" ;
                  : beep millis = "450"  pitch = "-26" ;
                   : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
    : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
      : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
       : beep millis = "400"  pitch = "-26" ;
       : beep millis = "400"  pitch = "-26" ;
         : beep millis = "225"  pitch = "-26";
          : beep millis = "225"  pitch = "-26" ;
                  : beep millis = "450"  pitch = "-26" ;
     
     
                : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
    : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
      : beep millis = "125"  pitch = "-26" ;
       : beep millis = "1100"  pitch = "-26"; 
         : beep millis = "1050"  pitch = "-19";
          : beep millis = "1000"  pitch = "-20";
          : beep millis = "950"  pitch = "-13";
          : beep millis = "1000"  pitch = "-14";
                     : beep millis = "950"  pitch = "-7";
       : beep millis = "950"  pitch = "-8";
          : beep millis = "1000"  pitch = "-1";

       : beep millis = "900"  pitch = "-2";
         : beep millis = "1000"  pitch = "5";

        : beep millis = "2000"  pitch = "4";
            : press_any_key ;
   
   
: clear_screen;

   : print "^c^-- Dawn of the Soviet Ladybirds  --";
   : print "^c^(A Cold War Coccinellidae Caper)" ;
   : print "\n^c^By Christopher Merriner" ;
   : print "\nJuly, 1950. The world balanced on a knife edge.  An Iron Curtain had descended across half the globe and on either side, newly-minted nuclear powers faced each other as the Cold War began to heat up. The Soviets had entrenched their position in Europe and declared Eastern Germany a Democratic Republic, North Korea had invaded the South, and across the Atlantic the Americans were busy sniffing out subversive elements from within the very State Department itself whilst busying themselves building the H-bomb. ";
   : print "Such things weighed heavily on the mind of middle-aged spinster Miss Dorothy Clutterbuck, as she tended to the roses in the garden of Willow Cottage. To have lived through all the privations of war and won the victory, only to be faced daily with ever greater peril! Why it was enough to test one's sanity. And then there were the ladybirds..." ;
    : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "What a summer for them it had been! Dorothy was ordinarily happy to see them in her garden, for they made short work of the greenfly besides being so gay and colourful. But this year there was such an abundance of  them that it really was rather alarming. They descended in vast numbers, clustering thickly on the window panes and blocking out the light inside the cottage, while outside they filled the air, buzzing around and piling up in great drifts along the sides of the lane. It was worse than the great ladybird plague of 1927 that had made such headlines at the time. Whatever could be causing it? It was a mystery." ;
  
   
: print "And so it was that Miss Clutterbuck was outside tending her plants, pausing every so often to disentangle another of the ubiquitous beetles from her hair, when she noticed something. On the shell of the ladybird crawling across her gardening glove, she thought she saw... but no, she must have been mistaken. It was due to the things preying on her mind. Nevertheless, she paused to carry the specimen into the potting shed so that she could have a closer look through her magnifying glass." ;

 : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
: print "Dorothy could hardly believe her eyes! It was no trick of the light, but plain to see. There, on the back of the ladybird, was emblazoned the unmistakable emblem of the Soviet Union: the hammer and sickle! Surely it must be some sort of natural phenomenon, a quirk in pigmentation that just happened to... " ;
: print "But then she scrutinised further and noticed that the creature's antennae looked most peculiar. Rather longer and thinner than usual, and of a silvery appearance. They looked, in fact, very much like radio aerials. " ;
: press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
: print "Dorothy cried out and dropped the magnifying glass; the ladybird, seeming almost to sense that its secret had been discovered, launched itself and flew off and out of the potting shed." ;
: print "Dorothy reeled. She felt quite faint. There could only be one explanation for what she had seen. The Communists were coming! These ladybirds must be the advance party, gathering intelligence for their Soviet controllers. How diabolically clever of them to hide in plain sight like that - just what she might have expected from what she'd read of their deviousness in the daily newspapers. She must warn the authorities without delay. England was once again in direst peril!" ;
: press_any_key ;
: clear_screen;
: print "Dorothy straight away telephoned the police station and told her news to the duty Sergeant, who took it very seriously and promised to inform his superiors. When nothing more happened after several hours, she called again. And then again. Five times that day she must have called the police and told them the details of what she had discovered, impressing upon them ever more desperately the urgency of the situation. Eventually, quite exhausted by all the excitement, she retired to bed.   " ;
: press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
: print "She was awoken the next morning by a knock at the door. She checked the clock. It was past 8. Goodness, she had slept late. Whatever was the matter with her?" ;
: print "She opened the door to be greeted by a serious-looking gentleman accompanied by two other tall and silent persons, all of whom insinuated themselves into her house without delay. Before she knew it, they were in the living room and the serious-looking gentleman was addressing Dorothy from the hearth-rug." ;
: press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
: print "He was a doctor, the man explained. He'd come to see how Dorothy was. He'd heard that she had been under rather a strain for a long time, what with the war and its aftermath, the rationing still carrying on, and having to manage the house and her affairs all on her own. It was hardly surprising that she'd had a little breakdown. It was nothing to be ashamed of. Perhaps it was time that she went away, for a little rest? To somewhere where they knew how to make people like Dorothy better... " ;
: press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
: print "And so it was that Dorothy found herself unwilling and alone in The Institute, a prison in all but name. She had resisted at first, but acquiescence was inevitable once they had stripped her of all her possessions and encouraged her to take her medication. And then time passed as though in a dream, with little memory of what had gone before and each day feeling newly strange. All that seemed left to her was her name. " ;
: press_any_key ;
: clear_screen;
: print "Dorothy did not know how long she had been a prisoner when, one morning, she woke to her senses and remembered. The Soviet ladybirds! THAT was why she had been sent there. She had discovered their plot and they had put her away before she could tell the world. But she just HAD to warn someone. Was it already too late?" ;
: print "There was only one way for Dorothy to find out..." ;

   : press_any_key ;
              
 }

   : store_random var = "codevar" ;
   
  : if (codevar<20) {
      : set_true "fiveonefiveseven" ;
      }
       : if (codevar>19&&codevar<40) {
      : set_true "ninefoursixone" ;
      }
       : if (codevar>39&&codevar<60) {
   : set_true "nineonethreeeoght" ;
      }
       : if (codevar>59&&codevar<80) {
      : set_true "seventhreefournine" ;
      }
       : if (codevar>79&&codevar<101) {
      : set_true "twotwosixfive" ;


  
   }
   
   
 : clear_screen;
 : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "-1" ;
  : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "0";
   : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "1";
    : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "2";
      : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "3";
       : print "\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n^c^Chapter 1\n\n\nIntrigue Before Breakfast" ;
      : pause "50" ;
      : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "3" ;
  : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "2";
   : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "1";
    : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "0";
      : beep millis = "50"  pitch = "-1";
   : press_any_key ;

   
}

locations {

   your_zedroom: location "Dorothy's room was pleasant and airy, if a little bare of furnishings. The old iron bedstead was tolerably comfortable, the plain wooden table standing alongside fulfilled its role in life with a minimum of fuss, and the window had no pretensions beyond being a hole in the wall. " graphic = "dorothys_room_day" ;
   
   corridor: location "The western end of the corridor exuded the familiar scent of institutional corridors the world over: faintly medicinal, with strong notes of furniture polish and a definite undertone of boiled cabbage."  graphic = "corridor_1"  ;
   
   corridor2 : location "Like its eastern and western neighbours, the middle section of the corridor was really nothing to write home about. There was a door to the north."graphic = "corridor_2"   ;
   
   corridor3 : location "If anything, the eastern end of the corridor failed to live up to the dubious promise of its cousins to the west. There was a door to the south." graphic = "corridor_3"  ;
   
   bobsroom : location "This bedroom was remarkably similar to Dorothy's own, though even more spartan: there was a bed, a window and nothing else."graphic = "bobs_room_day"  ;
   
   bathroom : location "The bathroom was furnished with a suite of impossibly heavy sanitary ware, designed as though for use of rhinoceroses. Despite this, it still displayed the scars of use by generations of the interned." graphic = "bathroom" ;
   
   landing : location "The landing was a small space at the head of a Brobdingnagian sweep of stairs so massive and dark that they might have been hewed out of basalt, for the exclusive use of ogres. Dorothy, hovering on their threshold, felt rather small and insignificant." graphic = "staircase_1"  ;
   
   hallway : location "The hallway was once the centre of a fine, Jacobean mansion that had withstood plague, fire and a civil war before succumbing at last to the depredations of the Ministry of Works. Every gloomy oaken surface seemed to exude a silent, impotent rage."graphic = "upper_hallway" ;
   
   hallway1 : location "This part of the hallway was as gloomy and dour as the other, although perhaps just a bit more smug: it had always been the less popular of the hallways and couldn't help but seem satisfied at the decline of its fancier neighbour. In truth, nobody cared about hallways these days."graphic = "upperhallway_1_day"  ;
   
   landing1 : location "This landing was very similar to all the other landings, only distinguished by an extremely threadbare rug that seemed in a slightly worse state of repair than the Turin shroud." graphic = "second_landing" ;
   
   corridor4 : location "The eastern end of the corridor was the start of a wainscotted tunnel that extended gloomily to the east. There was a door to the north." graphic = "1stfloorcorridor_start"  ;
   
   corridor5 : location "The middle of the corridor played a vital, if overlooked role in keeping the eastern and western parts separate. As with so many things, one would only appreciate it if it was suddenly to disappear. There was a door to the south."graphic = "1st_floor_corridor_mid"  ;
   
   corridor6 : location "Little daylight penetrated to the western end of the corridor, rendering it dark enough to grow mushrooms. There was an electric light but, as in all the other corridors, it remained perpetually unlit. There was a door to the north." graphic = "1stflrcorridorend"  ;
   
   landing2 : location "The second floor landing had airs above its station; in reality, it was no more grandiose than its more visited relative beneath." graphic = "1st_landing"  ;
   
   corridor7 : location "The corridor outside Ms Priam-Farl's office was unremarkable, though the floor was heavily scuffed, as though subject to the constant rushing to and fro of feet."graphic = "outside_secretary"   ;
   
   secretarys_office : location "Ms Priam-Farl's office was a tidy little nest of a room, from which all the really important business of The Institute was conducted, contrary to the delusions of the Director. Whilst weighty matters of great strategic importance were pored over in the office above, to no discernible effect, there below Ms Priam-Farl ensured that the gas and electricity bills were paid and that sufficient eggs arrived daily, for all the residents' breakfasts." graphic = "secretarys_office_calendar"  ;
   
   landing3 : location "The third floor landing had a lofty air, and not just because of its superior elevation. The balustrade was a little more polished up there, and the rug a little more expensive, although it did look as though some sort of animal had been shedding hairs all over it. "graphic = "toplanding" ;
   
   corridor8 : location "The corridor was unusually quiet, and there was a palpable schoolboy-outside-the-headmaster's-office sort of tension in the air."  graphic = "outside_directors" ;
   
   directors_office : location "Dr David Quelle's office was as inscrutable as the man himself, being furnished with nothing more than a high stool by the window and several enormous, blank canvases mounted on the walls. Dorothy wondered what on earth The Director did up there all day, whilst Ms Priam-Farl beavered away feverishly in the room beneath." graphic = "directors_office_closed" ;
   
   dining_room : location "The dining room had been built for the use of barons, and didn't appear at all happy at having being co-opted as a canteen for the riff-raff of The Institute. Vast and sooty portraits in oil glowered disapprovingly from on high as the slop was served out below." graphic = "dining_room_day" ;
   
   basket : location "It felt rather absurd and not a little unsavoury to be hiding in a laundry basket with a strange Russian gentleman, amongst masses of soiled laundry. But these were desperate times, the Soviet ladybirds were mustering and Dorothy knew that her rather erratic behaviour was somehow vital to the continued peace and security of Britain." ;
   
   laundry_room : location "The used laundry room had no aspirations beyond being a silo for dirty linen: it was bare and windowless, and the chute above admitted only the minimum of light, leaving everything shrouded in shadow. There was a distinct odour that reminded Dorothy of the pet dog she had loved as a child; that, and the warmth of the place made her feel oddly comforted."graphic = "laundry_room" ;
   
   downstairshallway : location "The downstairs hallway was a dark, mean little space, only fit for the orderlies. Dorothy imagined the generations of servants scurrying around these underground rooms, whilst their masters lorded it up above, and felt a tiny pang of socialist indignation, which startled her somewhat." graphic = "downstairs_hall"  ;
   
   caretakers_office : location "The Head Caretaker's Office had the distinctive feel of a place that wasn't much, but had been made the best of by a proud owner. It was spotlessly clean and tidy, with brushes and brooms lined up in a neat row, a bench with tools all tidily arranged, a desk with paper and pen that looked never to have been used, and a display of sink plungers of all different shapes and sizes, taking pride of place on the far wall." graphic = "caretakers_office_books" ;
   
   kitchen : location "The kitchen was Mrs Scurdle's private domain, a place of intrigue, gossip, illicit liaisons and, as a sort of side-line, the preparation of food. Every surface was dusted with flour, and on the stove a magmatic brown substance bubbled within what could only be described as a witch's cauldron."graphic = "kitchen"  ;
   
   passage : location "The servants' passage was a dark narrow tunnel, ideal for termites but a little unnerving for human beings to negotiate. Dorothy shuddered to think how many gallons of soup had been spilt there, en route to the dining room, across the centuries."graphic = "passage1"  ;
   
   passage1 : location "The dark, narrow passageway was barely worth describing, thought Dorothy to herself."graphic = "passage_2" ;
   
    vestibule : location "The vestibule was a lost looking neither-inside-nor-outside sort of space, with a cracked black and white tiled floor and a couple of moth-eaten umbrellas in a stand by the back door."  graphic = "vestibule" ;
   
   backpath : location "Immediately outside the back door was this path strewn with a small, sharp gravel that seemed especially designed to stick in the soles of slippers and discourage pedestrians. Nevertheless, inmates would doggedly suffer the path to access the garden beyond." graphic = "back_path"  ;

 
   lawn : location "The lawn was a lush expanse of unblemished, mattress-soft greenery, perfect for both walking and sitting on. Needless to say, walking or sitting on the grass was expressly forbidden." graphic = "lawn" ;
   
   shed : location "Boggart's shed was the nerve-centre of The Institute's gardening operations. It was extremely cluttered and  very homely, with enough surprising domestic touches (like sofa, radio, bathtub and gas stove) that Dorothy could not be certain that this was not in fact Boggart's permanent home." graphic = "shed"  ;
   
   wall : location "There was a high stone wall there, which Dorothy assumed must be concealing something interesting on the other side (to conceive of anything else was quite impossible). There really did seem to be a huge number of ladybirds in the area!" graphic = "wall" ;
   
    wall_1 : location "There was a high stone wall there, interrupted by an ostentatiously gothic archway blocked by an impenetrable-looking wooden door to the west (locked, and keyhole-less, for good measure). Everything there was thickly crusted with ladybirds. They seemed to favour this part of the garden."  graphic = "wall_archway" ;
    
    rose_garden : location "This rose garden was Boggart's life work, and his most prized possession. Luscious roses bloomed everywhere, their voluptuous velvety petals curling seductively in the sunshine and each bloom exuding a delicate and distinct scent as it swayed in the breeze." graphic = "rosegarden" ;
    
   }

######################################
#  Barriers                          #
######################################

barriers {
   
   door : door {
   
      from              = your_zedroom
      to                = corridor
      is_lockable       = true
      is_locked         = true
    key               = keyring
      show_blocked_exit = true
      on_unlock {
         
         : door_operation door = "door"  operation = "open_unlock" ;
         : print "Dorothy tried several of the keys on the keyring before finding the correct one and unlocking the door." ;
         
      }
      messages {
         bang_into_door                    = "The way was blocked by a locked door."
         cant_open_locked_door             = "The door had been locked."
         open                              = "Dorothy opened the door."
         cant_open_open_door               = "The door was already open."
         cant_close_closed_door            = "The door was already closed."
         unlock_door_with_what             = "But Dorothy did not have the key!"
         lock                              = Dorothy locked the door.
         
      }
      
   }
door2 : door {

   from              = corridor2
   to                = bobsroom
is_locked         = true
show_blocked_exit = true
on_unlock {
         
         : door_operation door = "door2"  operation = "open_unlock" ;
: print "Dorothy tried several of the keys and eventually found the one that unlocked the door." ;

      }
   key = keyring
   messages {
      bang_into_door = Bob's door had been locked.
      cant_open_locked_door = Bob's door had been locked.
      lock_door_with_what = But Dorothy did not have the correct key!
      
   }
   
}

passagedoor : door {

   from              = hallway1
   to                = passage1
   key               = random
   is_locked         = true
   show_blocked_exit = true
   messages {
   bang_into_door                    = Dorothy tried to, but there was a locked door in the way.
      cant_open_locked_door             = The door seemed to be locked and there was no keyhole visible.
      unlock_door_with_what             = Dorothy tried, but she could not see any keyhole.
      open                              = Dorothy opened the door.
      cant_unlock_already_unlocked_door = But the door was unlocked already!
      cant_open_open_door = The passage door was already open.
   }
   
}



   secretary_door : door {
   
      from              = corridor7
      to                = secretarys_office
      key               = keyring
show_blocked_exit = true

      on_unlock {
         
         : door_operation door = "secretary_door"  operation = "open_unlock" ;
: print "Dorothy tried several of the keys and eventually found the one that unlocked the door." ;

      }
       messages {
   bang_into_door                    = Dorothy tried to, but there was a locked door in the way.
      cant_open_locked_door             = The door was locked.
      unlock_door_with_what             = Dorothy tried, but she didn't have the key.
      open                              = Dorothy opened the door.
      cant_lock_open_door               = Dorothy would need to close the door before she could lock it.
      close                             = Dorothy closed the door.
      lock                              = Dorothy locked the door.
   }
   

}
vestibule_door : door {

   from              = hallway1
   to                = vestibule
   key               = random
   is_open           = true
   is_locked         = false
   show_blocked_exit = true
   messages {
   bang_into_door                    = The vestibule door had been locked.
   unlock_door_with_what             = Dorothy did not have the correct key!
   lock_door_with_what               =Dorothy did not have the correct key!
   cant_open_locked_door             = The door had been locked for the night.
   
   }
   
}
directors_door : door {

   from              = corridor8
   to                = directors_office
   key               = keyring
   show_blocked_exit = true
   on_unlock {
      
      : door_operation door = "directors_door"  operation = "open_unlock" ;
      : print "Dorothy tried several of the keys and eventually found the one that unlocked the door." ;
      
   }
   messages {
   bang_into_door                    = Dorothy tried to, but there was a locked door in the way.
      cant_open_locked_door             = The door was locked.
      unlock_door_with_what             = Dorothy tried, but she didn't have the key.
      open                              = Dorothy opened the door.
      unlock                            = Dorothy tried several of the keys and eventually found the one that unlocked the door.
      cant_lock_open_door               = Dorothy would need to close the door before she could lock it.
      close                             = Dorothy closed the door.
      lock                              = Dorothy locked the door.
   }
}

   location               = corridor8
   message                = The stoat rose up like a cobra and hissed viciously at Dorothy, waving its tiny, sharp-clawed paws threateningly in her direction. She dared not proceed any further!
block_when_exists      = stoat
}

The details of the 'accident' that had led to his confinement had never been disclosed to him, but his captors had hinted that it involved a stray dog, an inebriated opera singer and a brewery truck. subroutines {
   
   telltime : subroutine {

}


   }

   nursechat1 : subroutine {
      
      : if (linger()>2) {
      : store_random var = "nursecounter" ;
      
      : if (nursecounter<33) {
         : print "Nurse Brindle frowned. \"Take the medicine, Dorothy,\" she said, icily." ;
      }
      : if (nursecounter>32&&nursecounter<66) {
         : print "Nurse Brindle's expression was enough to wither foliage. \"The medicine,\" she said. \"Now, if you please.\"" ;
       }
       : if (nursecounter>65&&nursecounter<100) {
         : print "\"I can wait here all day if necessary!\" said Nurse Brindle, with a little too much relish." ;
       }
   }
   }
   badending : subroutine {
     
      : print "Dorothy felt as though there was something that she had missed, but she couldn't quite put her finger on what it was. It was as though she was on the way to an important revelation and suddenly the rug had been pulled out from beneath her. " ;
      : print "Everything seemed so futile! Soviet ladybirds - no one would ever believe her, however hard she tried to prove it. She was suddenly weary: sick and tired, perhaps, of the whole affair. And perhaps more than that." ;
       : beep millis = "100"  pitch = "-30" ;
: beep millis = "100"  pitch = "-31" ;
: beep millis = "100"  pitch = "-32" ;

        : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "She began to doubt herself. Could THEY have been telling her the truth all along? Was she really losing her marbles? Was the whole thing only in her mind? Maybe she should just stop fighting and take her medication as they asked her to. After all, it was probably for her own good. And then she could have a rest...a nice long rest...and forget about it all." ;
     : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "Later on, ensconced in her room, daybreak seemed an eternity away. Who knew what the dawn might bring?      : end_game;

   ladybirdstuff : subroutine {
: if (chance(10)) {
: if (!is_present "ladybird"){
: if (!is_present "soviet_ladybird") {
: set_integer var = "ladybirdtimer"  value = "5" ;

: store_random var = "randomvar" ;
   : if (randomvar<51) {
   : print "Out of the corner of her eye, Dorothy saw a ladybird whirr into view and land nearby." ;
   : create "ladybird" ;
   }
   : if (randomvar>50) {
    : print "Out of the corner of her eye, Dorothy saw a ladybird whirr into view and land nearby." ;
      : create "soviet_ladybird" ;
   }
}
}
}
 } 
 
    residents : subroutine {
: if (chance(6)) {
: if (is_at "backpath"||is_at "corridor"||is_at "corridor2"||is_at "corridor3"||is_at "corridor4"||is_at "corridor5"||is_at "corridor6"||is_at "dining_room"||is_at "hallway"||is_at "hallway1"||is_at "lawn"||is_at "vestibule"||is_at "wall"||is_at "wall_1") {
   : store_random var = "residents" ;
   : if (residents<25) {
      : print "An elderly gentleman shuffled past in his pyjamas. His eyes were wide and staring, but he seemed to see nothing." ;
      
   }
     : else_if (residents>24&&residents<51) {
      : print "A young couple strolled past in their nightclothes, chatting away about how fresh the air seemed on the pier, and how becalmed was the sea." ;
   
}
  : else_if (residents>50&&residents<75) {
      : print "A middle-aged bespectacled man wandered by, muttering something scientific-sounding in German." ;
}
: else {
  :if (residents>74&&residents<100) {
      : print "Two old ladies passed by, arguing fiercely over the relative merits of macaroons versus scones." ;
}
}
}
}

 } 
 
 bottling : subroutine {
    
: if (is_carried "pill_bottle") {
   : if (bottleopen) {
      : if (!ladybirdinbottle&&!svladybirdinbottle) {
       : print "Dorothy deftly encouraged the ladybird into the pill bottle, and fastened the lid." ;
         : set_false "bottleopen" ;
         : if (is_carried "ladybird") {
            : set_true "ladybirdinbottle" ;
            : increment "winstate" ;
            
         : destroy "ladybird" ;
         }
         : else {
            : set_true "svladybirdinbottle" ;
            : increment "winstate" ;
         : destroy "soviet_ladybird" ;
      }
      }
      : else {
      : print "But the bottle already contained a ladybird! Although they were in all probability agents of a hostile power, it seemed rather unfair to cram two of them into the tiny bottle. Besides, it was probably against the Geneva Convention.";
      }
   }
   : else {
         : print "Dorothy considered trapping it in the pill bottle - but the bottle was not open!" ;
         }
}
: else {
   : print "But Dorothy has nothing to capture a ladybird in!" ;
}


    
    
    
    
    
    
 }
 nursepillstuff : subroutine {
    
 
 
 :if (dissolvedpills&&!dissolvedtablets||dissolvedtablets&&!dissolvedpills) {
: if (!message) {
: print "Dorothy witnessed Nurse Brindle sipping the drugged tea, but it seemed to have little effect. She must have had the constitution of a buffalo! Perhaps a different blend was needed?" ;
: set_true "message" ;
}
}
: if (!nurseknockout&&dissolvedpills&&dissolvedtablets) {
: if (!message) {
 : print "Dorothy witnessed Nurse Brindle sipping the drugged tea and waited long minutes while nothing at all happened. Why, the woman was so resistant her insides must have been ceramic! But eventually, even the Nurse could not help but succumb to the heavy dose of sedatives; her head began to nod, the sentimental memoir of a murder slipped from her fingers, and presently she was fast asleep." ;
   : set_true "nurseknockout" ;
   : set_true "message" ;
   }
   }
 }

 catchstoat : subroutine {
 : if (is_present "stoat") {
      : if (is_beside "cutlery_box") {
         : if (cutleryboxopen) {
            : if (meatinbox) {
               : print "Dorothy placed the cutlery box on its side, with the open lid forming a ramp and ensured that the rabbit meat was placed deep within. To the outside observer this may have seemed like the actions of a lunatic but Dorothy was quite assured of her faculties in this. Her grandfather had been a gamekeeper, and had passed onto his granddaughter much useful lore on the trapping of stoats and other such vermin, in antique cutlery boxes." ;
               : press_any_key ;
            : clear_screen;
            : print "The stoat approached warily, clearly smelling a rat as well as the rabbit but unable to prevent its instinct for fresh meat from overcoming its caution. It glared at Dorothy almost resentfully as it disappeared into the box, retrieved the meat and made to leave...but  before it could do so, Dorothy quickly slammed the lid shut on the thing and turned the box door to the floor. The stoat squealed and scratched within, but there was no escape." ;
               : destroy "stoat" ;
               : set_false "cutleryboxopen" ;
               : set_true "ferretinbox" ;
               : press_any_key ;
               : redescribe;
               
            }
            : else {
            : print "Dorothy realised that she would need some sort of bait to lure the stoat into a trap. Stoats had no natural curiosity concerning antique cutlery boxes!";
            }
         }
         : else {
         : print "Dorothy realised that the cutlery box would need to be open before anything could be lured inside it." ;
         }
      }
      : else_if (is_carried "cutlery_box") {
         : print "Dorothy realised that she would need to leave the cutlery box on the floor to have any hope of trapping anything inside it!" ;
      }
      : else {
         : print "But Dorothy did not have a suitable container to trap anything in" ;
      }
      }
      
   
   

    
 }

   : print "The door closed behind him, and Dr Quelle turned to them both. \"A satisfactory conclusion to this whole affair, I am sure you will agree,\" he stated coldly whilst stroking the stole; Dorothy could have sworn that she saw the tail of the thing twitch. \"And now, Miss Clutterbuck and Colonel Bobrinsky, you must prepare to leave us. At once. Gather your things please. A car will be waiting downstairs for you in half an hour.\"";

   : clear_screen;

   : press_any_key ;
   : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   
   : print "\n It didn't take long for them to pack. Practically all their possessions had been taken from them when then arrived and there seemed little hope of retrieving them. And so they left The Institute empty handed and in their nightclothes, Dorothy with nothing but her watch, and Bob his spectacles, and stepped into the waiting car. As they drove away from The Institute and through the countryside, Dorothy half expected the silent chauffeur to turn off the road and into a deserted quarry, there to dispatch the pair of them with least fuss. Dorothy did not feel much perturbed by the prospect: it would be just another on the end of a long line of absurdities, but at least a final one. She glanced at Bob staring vacantly out of the window and realised that the thought had not even occurred to him. She wondered if he had really ever recovered his senses. Perhaps he never had them in the first place?" ;
     : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "But no such excitement occurred, and within an hour the pair were deposited unceremoniously at an unfamiliar railway station, the name of which neither of them had ever heard of. They had no money between them, but somehow managed to make their way back towards London through the goodwill of a benevolent train conductor who assumed, quite rightly, that the pair had escaped from a madhouse. They didn't speak much on the way. There wasn't a lot to say. But when it was time to depart Bob held Dorothy's hand for a very long time and seemed reluctant to leave, before she finally persuaded him to unclasp her and sent him on his way. Poor man. She did hope that he would be alright. Perhaps they would meet again some day?" ;
   : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   
   : print "Later that evening, she sat in the living room of Willow Cottage with a small sherry and went over the events of the past two days. It was all so muddled! She didn't know where to start or what to believe. Could it be that she had simply dreamt the whole thing and had never left the walls of her cottage? It certainly looked as though she had never been away. Perhaps a little too much sherry the evening before had returned to haunt her in the night.";
     : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   :print "But no! There had been a plot and she had foiled it, of that she was sure. Those Soviet ladybirds were real, she had seen them! And, beetles or no beetles, they were sure to try again. Nothing and nowhere was safe from the Bolshevik menace; England's green fields were under threat from a red tide; one way or another, the Communists were coming. And when they did, she, ever brave, ever vigilant Miss Dorothy Clutterbuck would be there on the front line, ready to turn them back." ;
   : print "\n That was, if it was not already too late..." ;
   : print "\n\n\n^c^THE END?" ;
 
       : press_any_key ;     
        :end_game;

 : print "Dorothy sat by the fire in the cosy living room of Willow Cottage and partook of a small sherry.    : press_any_key ;

The shiny red carapaces glittered in the weakening sunlight and rattled and clattered across one another like so many empty nutshells." ;
      : press_any_key ;

That was the purpose of the modified antennae: the ladybirds were to have simultaneously broadcast a jamming signal, crippling communications, rendering useless the British radar system and preventing millions of avid listeners from tuning in to Tommy Handley on the radio. The chaos would have been absolute!";

It was a bluff - they were helpless against such a diabolical scheme - but it worked. : match "load-"  {
    : print "Choose a slot below or, to load from file, quite this menu with #4 and type LOADF." ;
    :load;
}

: match "save-"  {
    : print "Choose a slot below or, to save to file, quite this menu with #4 and type SAVEF." ;
    :load;
}

   : print "Dorothy had more pressing things to do right now than moving that around." ;

: match "stand _"  {
: print "Dorothy didn't much fancy standing on that." ;

: match "instructions-"  {

: clear_screen;

   : print "--INSTRUCTIONS--" ;
   : print "SETTING" ;
   : print "Dawn of the Soviet Ladybirds is a text-based adventure game, set during the Cold War. You play Dorothy Clutterbuck, a middle-aged spinster with a paranoid ladybird fixation, and your goal is to escape from The Institute and warn the world about…whatever it is that you think is going on." ;
   : print "CONTROLLING THE GAME" ;
   : print "You control the game by entering simple commands in English, in verb-noun format, eg ‘GET LAMP’, ‘THROW STONE’, ‘UNTIE ROPE’. Many, but not all commands are understood; the game will tell you if it doesn’t know what you are talking about. " ;
   : print "NAVIGATION" ;
   : print "Exits are listed in each location." ;
   : print "Use ‘EAST, WEST, NORTH, SOUTH, NORTHEAST, NORTHWEST, SOUTHEAST, SOUTHWEST, UP, DOWN’ to move in the available direction. These can be abbreviated to ‘N, S’ etc." ;
   : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   
: print "INTERACTING WITH OBJECTS" ;
   : print "Use:\n- ‘EXAMINE’ (object) (abbreviated ‘X’) to examine an object eg EXAMINE CAR.\n- ‘INVENTORY’ (abbreviated ‘I’) to see what you are carrying.\n- ‘GET’ (object) to get an object (but note that there is a limit to how much you can carry) eg GET BAG.\n- ‘READ’ (object) to read something readable eg READ MAGAZINE.\n- ‘DROP’ (object) to drop an object eg DROP CALCULATOR.\n- ‘OPEN’ (object) to open something openable eg OPEN SHOEBOX.\n- ‘CLOSE’ (object) to close something closeable eg CLOSE DUSTBIN.\n- ‘ENTER’ (object) to enter something large enough to get into eg ENTER WARDROBE." ;
      : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "\nINTERACTING WITH PEOPLE" ;: print "There are plenty of different characters in the game, all of whom can be talked to.\n Use:\n- ‘TELL’ (the particular character) to tell them something, eg TELL HARRY.\n- ‘ASK’ (a particular character) to ask them something, eg ASK SARAH. \nThese commands are context dependent: due to the verb-noun input you can’t ask or tell a character about a specific thing, but in the right place and at the right time, you will get a sensible (and often important) response.\n* NOTE: sometimes a character will have a lot to say to you. If it seems like the conversation has not ended then you may need to ASK and/or TELL several times (as in real life) to carry on the conversation. If there is nothing else to say when you try to ASK or TELL then the game will say so.\n- ‘GIVE’ (object) to give a character something, eg GIVE SPOON.  Again, this command is context dependent. You can’t say who to give an object to, but in the right place and at the right time, the command will produce the desired result." ;
      : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "\nOTHER USEFUL COMMANDS" ;
   : print "This list is not exhaustive, but these commands are helpful and/or needed to play the game:\n- ‘TRAP’ or ‘CAPTURE’  (object) to trap a living creature (if you’ve got something to trap them in!), eg TRAP ELEPHANT.\n- ‘PUT’ (object) to put a non-living object somewhere, eg PUT BISCUITS. Again, this is context dependent. You can’t say where to put the object, but the command will work in the correct place and time.\n- ‘LOCK’ (object) to lock something, eg LOCK DOOR (but you’ll need to have the right key).\n- ‘UNLOCK’ (object) to unlock something eg UNLOCK DOOR (but you’ll need to have the right key).\n- ‘HIDE’ (object) to hide something somewhere eg HIDE CAULIFLOWER. Note that this command is to hide an object and won't work to hide yourself; if you want to do that, then you'll need to move to a place of concealment. \n* HINT – hiding something might be useful near the start of the game. *\n- ‘QUIT’ or ‘RESTART’ if you’ve really had enough.\n- ‘LOAD’ and ‘SAVE’ to load/save the game position to a save slot.\n- ‘LOADF’ and ‘SAVEF’ to load/save the game position from/to file." ;
      : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
   : print "--GAMEPLAY--" ;
   
   : print "CHAPTERS\nThe game is divided into ‘Chapters’, each set during a particular part of the day. To proceed to the next chapter, you will need to complete certain tasks. It's up to you to work out what they are!\n" ;
   : print "WINNING AND LOSING\nYou’ll need to have completed certain tasks within each chapter before you can progress to the next one. This means that it is very unlikely that you’ll get all the way to the end of the game only to realise that you should have done something right at the start. There are a couple of instances where you will not be able to progress if you miss a timed event (see below), or leave something in  the wrong place, but otherwise, you’ll usually get more than one chance to do what you need to do.\nTIMED EVENTS\n There are timed events in this game, but for the most part they are repeated - so if you miss them, you'll have another chance. There are two exceptions to this, both in Chapter 2. If you fail to do what is required during either of these timed events then the game is unwinnable and, mercifully, it will end a short time afterwards." ;
      : press_any_key ;
   : clear_screen;
: print "\nTIPS:\n -EXAMINE everything: you’ll often find something that you didn’t see at first glance, and at the very least, you’ll get a humorous (or baffling, depending on your sense of humour) response.\n- Make a note of what you have to do to complete each chapter. You may need to play a chapter through more than one before you figure out what you need to do.\n- SAVE frequently, particularly at the start of chapters in case you miss something critical and don't want to start again from the very beginning.\n- HINTS are available (enter 'HINT'). In the right place and at the right time, you will be given a clue that should help you to proceed.\n-If you need more help then STUCK will provide explicit guidance on what to do, but be warned that this will involve spoilers.\n- If you're still having trouble, or just want to praise me, curse me, or give feedback then I can be found at christopher.merriner@gmail.com" ;
: print "\nEnjoy the game!" ;
: press_any_key ;
: redescribe;

}
